    [Original] Brushing fraud: Britons told to beware of mystery parcels as new scam soars
    Receiving an unexpected parcel with your personal details could signal that your information has been compromised in a rising â€œbrushingâ€ fraud scheme, warns cybersecurity firm McAfee. Fraudsters obtain names, addresses, and other personal data through data breaches, then use them to place fake orders on online marketplaces under victimsâ€™ identities. The scam involves sending low-quality itemsâ€”such as cheap jewellery, key chains, homeware, or even plant seedsâ€”to unsuspecting recipients. These packages often arrive without prior order confirmation and may contain hidden risks, including harmful toys, unsafe cosmetics, or malicious items like QR codes or USB drives designed to install malware on devices. The fraudstersâ€™ goal is to generate fake verified reviewsâ€”typically five-star ratingsâ€”on the products they sell. These reviews, appearing to come from real customers, boost the sellerâ€™s credibility and search rankings, increasing sales. According to McAfeeâ€™s Oliver Devane, the legitimacy of these reviews depends on the product being delivered, making the physical shipment essential. While the scam appears victim-free, it exposes individuals to potential harm and indicates a data breach. Devane emphasizes that recipients should not use or consume the items, as their safety and origin are unknown. The packages typically arrive during peak shopping periods but can occur at any time. If you receive one, do not attempt to return it, as this may trigger further scam attempts. Instead, report the item to the marketplaceâ€”Amazon, for example, prohibits third-party sellers from sending unsolicited packages and provides a reporting mechanism. Check your online accounts for unauthorized activity and change passwords immediately. Enabling two-factor authentication is also recommended. If you identify fake reviews under your name, report them to the platform to help remove them. The key takeaway: treat the package as potentially dangerous, dispose of it safely, and take steps to secure your digital accounts.

    [Original] Could an Electronic Coach Help Ski Jumpers Leap Farther?
    On Monday, 24 Olympic ski jumpers will compete in the menâ€™s super team event at the Predazzo Ski Jumping Stadium in the Italian Alps, racing down a 378-foot slope at speeds exceeding 60 mph before leaping toward the world record of 146.5 meters (481 feet). The sport demands precise control of aerodynamics, with athletes relying on split-second adjustments in body position and pressure distribution to maximize lift and minimize drag. â€œA jump is a pretty complex thing that happens within 15 seconds,â€ said Christoph Leitner, a professor of electrical engineering at ETH Zurich. â€œThere is this narrow window of 300 milliseconds, which is the actual leap. And all the positioning, the center of mass, everything must be stable when you arrive to optimize your performance.â€ Recent controversies have highlighted the lengths athletes go to gain an edge: in January, Norwegian athletes and coaches were caught illegally adding stitching to speedsuits to increase surface area, while rumors persist of some injecting their penises to boost lift. In response, Leitner and his team have developed a wearable feedback system using sensors on ski boots that measure body position and pressure applied to the skis. Data is transmitted in real time to goggles worn by the jumper, displaying small red or green lights in the periphery to signal necessary adjustments. Coaches on the ground receive the same data on laptops, allowing them to identify issues like improper weight distribution or incorrect ski-body angles before a jump is completed. The system, presented at an IEEE conference in 2023, aims to translate complex sensor data into intuitive, non-distracting feedback. â€œWe have created a sensor system that collects data and is able to process this data and save the data and transfer it to the cloud or give feedback to the athlete,â€ Leitner said. The device is currently being tested by junior athletes and members of Switzerlandâ€™s â€œBâ€ team, with preliminary results showing performance improvements. Matheo KÃ¤ch, a coach and researcher at Swiss Ski, noted the system helps coaches understand the physical sensations athletes experience during jumps, which are otherwise subjective. The team hopes to expand the technology to other winter sports, such as biathlon, where stance optimization during shooting could be enhanced. The device is targeted for use in training ahead of the 2030 Winter Olympics in the French Alps.

    [Original] More Than Ever, Videos Expose the Truth. And Cloud It, Too.

    [Original] China moves deeper into liquid cooling as AI data centres push their thermal limits

Its Shenzhen-listed shares have more than tripled over the past year, closing at 113.14 yuan on Friday.

    [Original] How recent graduates entering the job market can outperform AI
    As automation erodes cognitive and interpersonal skills, those who embrace the struggle of enhancing offline reasoning will thrive Artificial intelligence (AI) is eroding the very capabilities young professionals need to remain valuable in a machine-automated era. That is the real challenge facing graduates entering the workforce. It is not simply a case of AI destroying jobs â€“ though it is â€“ but that it is undermining our cognitive and interpersonal skills. Hiring managers make decisions based on economics, not social good. They need to be convinced that a young human worker is a better investment than a machine. Many employers are reluctant to bet on people with no practical experience and no domain knowledge. Management may prefer to upskill experienced staff to use AI to do more of what they already do. A perceived preference for job-hopping among younger workers only compounds the disincentive. This conforms to our experience as a small company paying high Hong Kong rents. The â€œproductive struggleâ€ of thinking through hard problems, failing, retrying and eventually making breakthroughs has always been at the core of genuine learning. That this struggle is increasingly bypassed is what keeps educators and developmental psychologists awake at night. Itâ€™s also what troubles managers when junior staff expect work to be easy. The friction of navigating daily life, of developing street smarts, is being removed for AI natives.

    36Kr has learned that according to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in a further effort to facilitate personnel exchanges between China and foreign countries, China will implement a visa-free policy for ordinary passport holders from Canada and the United Kingdom starting February 17, 2026. Citizens of these two countries holding ordinary passports may enter China for business, tourism, visiting relatives and friends, exchanges, or transit without a visa, provided their stay does not exceed 30 days. This visa-free policy will be in effect until December 31, 2026.

    According to data from the Comprehensive Transportation Spring Festival Travel Season Work Group, on February 14, 2026 (the 13th day of the Spring Festival travel season, the 27th day of the 12th lunar month, Saturday), the total volume of inter-regional population movement across society reached 285.662 million person-times, a 0.8% decrease compared to the previous day, and a 7.5% increase compared to the same day in 2025 (Sunday). Among them, railway passenger volume was 15.299 million person-times, unchanged from the previous day, and a 5.3% increase compared to the same period in 2025.

    Hong Kong Special Administrative Region Financial Secretary Paul Chan said in a blog post on the 15th that the number of mainland Chinese tourists visiting Hong Kong during this year's Spring Festival holiday is expected to reach 1.43 million, with daily arrivals projected to rise by about 6% year-on-year. Chan noted that the number of visitors to Hong Kong has been steadily increasing since the beginning of the year, with a total of 7.23 million visitors from January 1 to February 13, a 9.6% increase compared to the same period last year, and overseas visitors showing a more significant increase of 16.4%. (Xinhua News Agency)

    [Original] Andrew's time as trade envoy should be investigated, says Vince Cable
    Former UK trade envoy Andrew Mountbatten-Windsor should face a criminal investigation over allegations of corruption, said Sir Vince Cable, former secretary of state for business and trade. Documents released by the US Department of Justice indicate Mountbatten-Windsor forwarded sensitive UK government information, including commercial data and reports from official visits, to convicted sex offender Jeffrey Epstein. Cable called the conduct â€œtotally unacceptableâ€ and urged a police or Director of Public Prosecutions (DPP) review to determine if criminal corruption occurred, alongside a government inquiry into how such breaches were permitted. Mountbatten-Windsor served as UK trade envoy from 2001 to 2011, enjoying privileged access to senior government and business figures globally. In 2010, he shared an email exchange with David Stern, who passed it to Epstein. The email, from investment banker Terence Allen in Abu Dhabi, detailed RBSâ€™s restructuring plans, critical remarks about CEO Stephen Hester, and internal conflicts at Aston Martin. RBS was then majority state-owned. It remains unclear whether this information originated from his official role, as Mountbatten-Windsor was also an RBS customer. The same year, he allegedly forwarded government reports from visits to Vietnam, Singapore, and China to Epstein. Additional emails suggest he passed Treasury information about Iceland to banker Jonathan Rowland. Official guidance requires trade envoys to maintain confidentiality over sensitive political, commercial, or diplomatic information. Thames Valley Police confirmed they have consulted Crown Prosecution Service specialists regarding the allegations. Labour MP Sarah Owens called for Mountbatten-Windsor to face questioning by both police and Parliament, while colleague Rachael Maskell accused him of being â€œconservative with the truth.â€ Maskell urged that he be stripped of his succession rights and role as a councillor of state, stating that â€œall of these titles and positions need to be addressedâ€ so he is held fully accountable as a citizen. The King expressed â€œprofound concernâ€ over the allegations, and Buckingham Palace stated it stands â€œready to supportâ€ law enforcement if approached. Mountbatten-Windsor, facing mounting pressure to testify in the US regarding his ties to Epstein, recently relocated from his Windsor home to the Sandringham Estate in Norfolk. The latest US documents also include images of him, fully clothed, kneeling on all fours over a woman, further intensifying scrutiny.

    [Original] Could Manchester be a model for the UK to kickstart growth?
    Manchester is defying the UKâ€™s sluggish economic trend, with a decade of sustained 3.1% annual growthâ€”double the national averageâ€”driven by decades-long strategic investment and cross-party political support. Once known for decline, the city now buzzes with development: cranes dot the skyline, new skyscrapers rise, and the city centreâ€™s population has surged from 500 in 1990 to an estimated 100,000, with projections of 250,000 by 2035. The University of Manchester, the UKâ€™s most popular institution for applications, provides a critical mass of talent, while major employers like Bank of New York, IBM, Booking.com, and GCHQ have anchored a thriving knowledge economy. This has spurred growth in services, hospitality, and innovation, with companies like Hip Pop citing Manchesterâ€™s vibrant food and drink scene as ideal for testing new products. The Metrolink tram system now sets record ridership levels, and the delayed opening of a new music arena has instead boosted week-round hospitality demand. Mayor Andy Burnham highlights a reversal in the historic â€œnorth-southâ€ migration, with 13,000 Londoners moving to Greater Manchester in 2024â€”more than the 11,800 who moved south. This net inflow reflects growing appeal, fueled by affordable city-centre living, a world-class music scene, and improved transport. Productivity has soared: Manchesterâ€™s GVA per capita reached Â£61,589 in 2023, nearly tripling since 2000. Burnham credits long-term devolution, including powers over transport and skills, and consistent backing from central governments across party lines. Business leaders note the importance of coordinated public-private efforts and strategic planning. Yet challenges remain: homelessness affects 1 in 61 residentsâ€”higher than most UK cities outside Londonâ€”highlighting the strain of rapid development. Additionally, growth is concentrated in the city centre, raising concerns about equitable distribution across Greater Manchesterâ€™s wider towns and villages. Efforts to expand Manchesterâ€™s global profile include a Great North Olympic bid, backed by cross-party mayors, challenging the notion that only London can host major international events. While experts like Andy Spinoza acknowledge Manchesterâ€™s â€œunique handâ€â€”a mix of devolution, a major airport, universities, and cultural assetsâ€”caution that replication elsewhere is limited by differing local conditions. Still, the cityâ€™s success underscores the power of long-term vision, ambition, and inclusive economic strategy. As Burnham notes, Manchester proves that growth is possible when cities act with purpose beyond Westminsterâ€™s daily turbulence.

    [Original] Gender pay gap won't close for another 30 years, warns trade unions group
    ShareSaveJosh MartinShareSavePA MediaThe gender pay gap is prominent even in industries where women make up the majority of employees, such as health and social careMoves to close the gender pay gap will not be successful until 2056 if progress remains at its current rate, according to the Trades Union Congress (TUC). The disparity between average wages for men and women is 12.8%, or Â£2,548 per year, according to TUC analysis of official pay data. It is widest in the finance and insurance industry, at 27.2%. In the leisure service sector it was only 1.5%. The gender pay gap measures the difference in salaries paid to men and women in the same industries. Employers with more than 250 UK staff must report pay data. The government said it was "tackling the root causes of the gender pay gap and backing women to succeed at work". Even in industries where woman make up a majority of the workforce, such as education and health and social care, the gender pay gaps are 17% and 12.8%, respectively. Pay disparity between genders meant that the average woman employee "effectively works for 47 days of the year for free," the TUC said. "Women have effectively been working for free for the first month and a half of the year compared to men," TUC general secretary Paul Nowak said. "With the cost of living still biting hard, women simply can't afford to keep losing out. They deserve their fair share". Nowak pointed to the recent Employment Rights Act as a "an important step forward for pay parity" but said the government needed to increase access to paid parental leave so "mums and dads can better share care". The gender pay gap is widest for workers aged 50-59, which the group of unions argues is partly due to the long-term effects of women pausing or reducing their career ambitions and pay to prioritise caring responsibilities. The TUC, the national federation of trade unions, wants improved access to flexible working and better access to childcare in order to help close the gap. Throughout the debate around increasing worker rights under the Employment Rights Act business groups argued that increased benefits and leave provisions would increase their costs and reduce their willingness to hire staff. "The cost of doing business is already leading to firms cutting jobs. With major changes to employment laws coming down the line, the government must be extra careful not to add to those pressures," said Matthew Percival, the Future of Work and Skills Director at business group the CBI. Employers will soon have to publish plans for how they plan to reduce the gender pay gap. A government spokesperson said: "Combined with changes to flexible working, stronger protections for expectant and new mothers, and wider action to review parental leave and to expand childcare entitlements, we are tackling the root causes of the gender pay gap and backing women to succeed at work."

    [Original] Trump Administration Ends Credit for Start-Stop Feature in Cars
    The Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) announced on Thursday that manufacturers will no longer earn credits for installing start-stop enginesâ€”systems that automatically shut off and restart vehicles at stopsâ€”to meet federal emissions standards. The move, part of the Trump administrationâ€™s broader effort to roll back fuel efficiency regulations, eliminates the â€œoff-cycleâ€ credits program, which had allowed automakers to count real-world emission-reducing technologies toward compliance. These credits previously applied to vehicles with model years 2012 and later, and were used to offset greenhouse gas emissions that exceeded regulatory limits. EPA Administrator Lee Zeldin cited concerns over battery degradation and widespread consumer dissatisfaction, stating in a news release that he heard from â€œcountless Americansâ€ who â€œpassionately advocatedâ€ for the featureâ€™s removal. He also noted in May 2025 that the administration was working to eliminate the credit, which he claimed â€œeveryone hates.â€ Despite these claims, experts, including Consumer Reports, have dismissed the battery damage concern as a misconception. Start-stop technology was introduced in 2012 to incentivize fuel savings and emissions reductions. While complaints peaked in 2022â€”with over 1% of all auto defect reports related to the feature, particularly in 2017 modelsâ€”complaints dropped nearly in half by 2024 despite broader adoption. Some drivers oppose the system due to perceived fuel savings inefficiencies or engine wear, though most vehicles allow temporary disabling of the feature. Research from SAE International in 2023 found that start-stop systems improved fuel economy by 7.27% to 26.4% under various driving conditions. The EPA also rejected the long-standing â€œendangerment finding,â€ a scientific determination from nearly 17 years ago that climate change endangers human health and the environment, which had underpinned regulations on carbon dioxide, methane, and four other greenhouse gases. The administration dismissed the finding as â€œhaving no basis in fact.â€ The off-cycle credit elimination also affects other technologies, including waste heat recovery and reflective paint. John Bozzella, CEO of the Alliance for Automotive Innovation, said the change corrected â€œsome of the unachievable emissions regulations enacted under the previous administration.â€ While the credit is now gone, manufacturers may still install start-stop systems. The policy shift underscores the administrationâ€™s push to ease vehicle emissions rules, even as transportation remains the largest source of U.S. greenhouse gas emissions.

    [Original] Like Trump, U.S. Embassies Are Raising Cash for Lavish July Fourth Parties
    President Trump announced in December a campaign to mark Americaâ€™s 250th birthday with â€œthe most spectacular birthday party the world has ever seen,â€ prompting U.S. embassies and consulates worldwide to aggressively solicit corporate donations for celebratory events. In Singapore, U.S. Ambassador Anjani Sinha hosted a high-profile, five-course dinner at the Capella Singaporeâ€”site of the 2018 Trump-Kim summitâ€”where he urged executives from companies including Citibank, Coinbase, Harley-Davidson, and 3M to contribute, saying, â€œI need your money.â€ Sinha claimed another embassy had raised $37 million and challenged Singaporeâ€™s business leaders, stating, â€œSingapore is a better country than that,â€ and implying local executives could do more. Attendees were told the funds would support events like an American rodeo, a Rockefeller Christmas tree lighting, and a gift to the Singapore Zoo. The event was sponsored by the American Chamber of Commerce in Singapore, Philip Morris, and the Milken Institute, which paid $5,000 to the hotel but denied donating to Freedom 250 or America250. Similar efforts are underway in Japan, where the embassy announced over 70 cultural, educational, and sporting events, including snow sculptures in Hokkaido. The missionâ€™s donor list includes Toyota Motor and SoftBank Group, with some companies contributing $1 million or more. U.S. Ambassador George Glass wrote to donors, stating President Trump had tasked him with making Japanâ€™s celebration â€œthe greatest celebration in the world outside of the United States.â€ The fundraising is being conducted through America250, a nonprofit created in 2016, and Freedom 250, a group backed by Trump allies that promotes events like an IndyCar race in Washington and an UFC match on the White House lawn. While Freedom 250 claims it was not involved in the Singapore dinner and does not accept foreign funding, the eventâ€™s follow-up document bore the Freedom 250 logo and listed planned â€œmarquee events.â€ The State Department stated it has policies governing fundraising for the anniversary, with donations supporting multiple programs. However, former diplomats like Ted Osius and Blair Hall criticized the scale, calling it unprecedented and damaging to perceptions of ethical governance. Osius, who raised tens of thousands for July Fourth events in Vietnam, said such large-scale solicitations risk creating the impression that access is for sale. Hall, who raised around $200,000 in similar events, called the current campaign â€œaberrantâ€ and said it undermines longstanding U.S. values on transparency and integrity. The American Chamber of Commerce in Singapore said the celebrations, coinciding with 60 years of U.S.-Singapore relations, reflect the best of American culture.

    Emerald Fennellâ€™s reimagined â€œWuthering Heights,â€ starring Margot Robbie and Jacob Elordi, debuted to an estimated $82 million globallyâ€”$40 million in the U.S. and Canada and $42 million overseasâ€”according to Warner Bros., which distributed the film.     [Original] Will 2026 Be the Year of the â€˜Soonicornâ€™?
    Once a rare milestone, the â€œunicornâ€ â€” a privately held start-up valued at over $1 billion â€” has become increasingly common, with more than 1,000 such companies now existing. The term, coined in 2013 by Aileen Lee of Cowboy Ventures, has expanded to include â€œdecacornsâ€ (valued at $10 billion or more) and â€œhectocornsâ€ (over $100 billion), while â€œsoonicornsâ€ describe start-ups valued between $500 million and $999 million. Ilya A. Strebulaev, a Stanford professor specializing in finance and venture capital, notes that more than 2,000 U.S. companies achieved soonicorn status by the end of last year â€” a dramatic increase from a decade ago. Though he did not coin the term, Strebulaev has become a leading proponent, emphasizing that soonicorns reflect a companyâ€™s current valuation rather than a guaranteed future as a unicorn. He anticipates 2026 to be a pivotal year, driven in part by the artificial intelligence boom, which has lowered barriers to high-valuation funding. Many new firms founded in recent years could reach soonicorn status this year, with some securing first-round funding at $500 million or more. Despite the â€œsoonâ€ in the name, Strebulaev cautions that not all soonicorns will become unicorns; some may go public at lower valuations, remain private, or fail entirely. The pace of growth has accelerated: while it once took an average of 6.5 years to reach unicorn status before 2015, the past decade has seen that drop to about 3.5 years. Additionally, large start-ups now often remain private longer, capitalizing on stable private funding amid volatile public markets. However, this trend may shift in 2026, as major private firms like Anthropic, OpenAI, and SpaceX â€” all hectocorns â€” are reportedly preparing for public offerings. The evolving landscape of â€œcornsâ€ reflects broader shifts in venture capital, innovation cycles, and market dynamics.

    [Original] What C.E.O.s Are Worried About
    Chief executives face an increasingly complex landscape in the second year of President Trumpâ€™s second term, navigating shifting tariffs, unpredictable trade policies, and heightened political engagement. At the World Economic Forum in Davos, top executives highlighted growth challenges amid a global economy averaging 3% growthâ€”insufficient for most companies seeking meaningful expansion. Rich Lesser of Boston Consulting Group emphasized the difficulty of finding growth, particularly in consumer-challenged markets. Jeremy Allaire of Circle stressed the need for long-term strategic thinking, urging leadership to balance immediate demands with future-oriented investments. Julie Sweet of Accenture noted that nearly every current business challenge stems from growth constraints. Artificial intelligence has emerged as a central concern, with leaders balancing innovation against workforce disruption. Bipul Sinha of Rubrik described the CEOâ€™s role as harmonizing geopolitics, AI risks, job displacement, and training into a cohesive growth strategy. Antonio Neri of Hewlett Packard Enterprise underscored the need for tech leaders to educate government officials at all levels to ensure effective, informed policy-making. John Q. Doyle of Marsh predicted that by year-end, companies will have clearer insights into AIâ€™s ROI, with priorities focused on workforce adoption and leveraging AI for growth. While some executives prioritize technology, others emphasize people. Zak Brown of McLaren Racing, a Formula 1 team, stated that despite AIâ€™s potential, his primary focus remains on culture and team retention. Hemant Taneja of General Catalyst advised companies to proactively manage workforce reductions caused by AI, urging businesses to be part of the solution rather than leaving the burden to society. Juvencio Maeztu of Ingka Group, operator of global IKEA stores, stressed authenticity in leadership as essential to building trust and a resilient culture. Stephen J. Ubl of PhRMA noted that this administration actively engages with CEOs, requiring greater political involvement than in past decades. As uncertainty persists, executives agree that success hinges on balancing long-term vision with immediate pressures, managing AI responsibly, and maintaining authentic leadership amid rapid change.

    [Original] Software? No Way. Weâ€™re an A.I. Company Now!
    When ChatGPT launched in November 2022, Intercom co-founder and CEO Eoghan McCabe faced an existential threat: if AI chatbots could handle customer service, companies might abandon help desksâ€”and the software that powered them. Within months, Intercom pivoted to an AI-first model, launching an AI customer service agent that now generates nearly $100 million in annual recurring revenue. McCabeâ€™s success reflects a broader industry panic. Over the past year, software stocks have plummeted, with the S&P North American Expanded Technology Software Index down 20% in a month and giants like Salesforce and ServiceNow shedding over 40% in value. J.P. Morgan reports $2 trillion in market capitalization lost since the peak, driven by rapid AI advancements like Anthropicâ€™s Claude Opus 4.6. The shift has triggered an identity crisis across the software sector. Once the dominant model, Software as a Service (SaaS), is being upended. Nearly all venture-backed software startups now tout AI, with 135 of 151 Y Combinatorâ€™s latest cohort identifying as AI companies. Half of all venture capital in 2023 went to AI startups, per CB Insights. Yet many efforts are superficialâ€”rebranding domains to â€œ.ai,â€ updating landing pages, but offering no real AI integration. Investors like Byron Deeter of Bessemer Venture Partners say such â€œAI wrappersâ€ are easily disrupted. Jasper, once valued at $1.5 billion, saw its valuation collapse after users bypassed it for direct access to OpenAIâ€™s models. Despite the frenzy, analysts caution against overreaction. J.P. Morgan argues markets are pricing in worst-case AI disruption scenarios unlikely to materialize in the next six months. Deeter emphasizes that AI models need software to monetizeâ€”â€œtheyâ€™re not a business in and of themselves.â€ Even AI-powered coding tools still require software for UI, backend, and cloud deployment. Tony Wang of 500 Global notes that the AI startup cycle is now so fast that interest can vanish within 18 months. Meanwhile, broader developments include the Trump administrationâ€™s repeal of the 2009 EPA finding that greenhouse gases endanger public health, erasing a key climate regulation foundation. Economic data showed strong January employment and easing inflation, though nearly 40% of growth last year came from AI data center spending.     [Original] T.S.A. Workers Brace for Another Shutdown They Didnâ€™t Cause
    When the Department of Homeland Security ran out of funding early Saturday, Transportation Security Administration (T.S.A.) employees faced another government shutdown, working without pay amid a congressional impasse over immigration enforcement policies. This marks the second major shutdown in less than a year, following a 43-day closure that left many T.S.A. workers financially devastatedâ€”some evicted, others unable to afford gas, medicine, or childcare. Many are still angry they did not receive a promised $10,000 bonus from Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem for â€œexemplary serviceâ€ during the prior shutdown. Roberto Echeverria, a lead transportation security officer at Salt Lake City International Airport and union member, said colleagues had been preparing for weeks, maximizing overtime to cushion the blow of missing their first full paycheck in about two weeks. T.S.A. employees in the Salt Lake region earn between $36,480 and $49,920 annually, depending on location. â€œHow many more times am I going to be able to do this?â€ Echeverria asked, noting nearly 100 officers left the Salt Lake team since the last shutdown. Union leaders say the financial strain disproportionately affects T.S.A. workers, who are unpaid while immigration enforcement personnel continue to receive pay through a separate fund. Rebecca Wolf, president of the American Federation of Government Employees T.S.A. Local 1127, said the agency is â€œpunishedâ€ for political gridlock. The union is also fighting a Trump administration effort to strip T.S.A. of collective bargaining rightsâ€”a move halted by a judge last month, though the threat remains. The financial hardship could directly impact travelers. Ha Nguyen McNeill, T.S.A.â€™s senior official performing the administratorâ€™s duties, warned that lack of childcare or other stressors could lead to last-minute absences, causing longer checkpoint lines, missed flights, and broader economic ripple effects. Travelers are already anxious, with recent flight suspensions in El Paso adding to concerns about aviation stability. No word has been given on whether bonuses will be awarded after this shutdown, despite the agencyâ€™s claim they were for â€œextraordinary effortsâ€ like working extra shifts. William Kincaid, a lead officer in Helena, Montana, said the lack of clear rules made the process feel like â€œa contest where you donâ€™t know the rules.â€ Employees report minimal guidance from management beyond being told not to wear uniforms in public after an incident in Los Angeles where T.S.A. officers were mistaken for ICE agents. â€œWeâ€™re just helping people get through the airport so they can go on a trip,â€ Kincaid said. The uncertainty over pay, schedules, and future bonuses continues to weigh heavily on a workforce bearing the brunt of political stalemate.

    [Original] Iran ready to discuss compromises to reach nuclear deal, minister tells BBC in Tehran
    Iranâ€™s deputy foreign minister, Majid Takht-Ravanchi, told the BBC in Tehran that Iran is ready to make compromises on its nuclear program if the U.S. demonstrates sincerity in lifting sanctions, placing the onus on Washington to prove its commitment. Speaking ahead of a second round of indirect talks in Geneva, Takht-Ravanchi stated, â€œThe ball is in Americaâ€™s court,â€ emphasizing that Iran is open to discussing uranium enrichment levels, including diluting its 60%-enriched stock, and potentially shipping out its 400kg of highly enriched uraniumâ€”similar to the 2015 deal. Russia has offered to accept the material again, as it did in the past. Iran has also proposed temporarily suspending enrichment, though Takht-Ravanchi said it was too early to confirm specifics. He denied that zero enrichment remains a sticking point, stating it â€œis not on the table anymore,â€ contradicting U.S. President Donald Trumpâ€™s recent assertion that â€œwe donâ€™t want any enrichment.â€ Iran insists negotiations focus solely on the nuclear file, rejecting demands to discuss its ballistic missile program or regional activities, which the U.S. and Israel have tied to any deal. Takht-Ravanchi criticized Trumpâ€™s recent remarks calling for regime change and encouraging protesters, calling them â€œan incitement to violence,â€ while reaffirming Iranâ€™s distinction between peaceful protest and violent unrest. He also questioned the U.S. military buildup in the region, warning that another war would be â€œtraumatic, bad for everybody,â€ and reiterated that U.S. bases in the region would be legitimate targets. Iran has accused Israel of undermining negotiations, citing its surprise attack in June that triggered a 12-day conflict just before planned talks. Iranian officials remain skeptical due to inconsistent U.S. messaging and past broken understandings, though the presence of Jared Kushner at recent talks was seen as a positive sign. Despite tensions, Takht-Ravanchi expressed hope for progress, urging the U.S. to show genuine intent. The BBCâ€™s Lyse Doucet, reporting from Tehran, is restricted from using her material on the BBCâ€™s Persian Service, a condition applying to all international media in Iran.

    [Original] Russia killed opposition leader Alexei Navalny using dart frog toxin, UK says
    Russian opposition leader Alexei Navalny was killed using epibatidine, a neurotoxin derived from poison dart frogs native to northern South America, according to a joint statement by the UK, France, Germany, Sweden, and the Netherlands. Two years after Navalnyâ€™s death in a Siberian penal colony on 16 February 2024 at age 47, the allies concluded that only the Russian state had the means, motive, and opportunity to carry out the poisoning. Navalny had been imprisoned for three years on fabricated charges and was transferred to the Arctic penal colony shortly before his death.

    [Original] US attorney general criticised after saying all Epstein files have been released
    The U.S. Department of Justice (DoJ) has declared it has fully complied with the Epstein Files Transparency Act, releasing all records, documents, communications, and investigative materials related to nine specified categories. In a letter to Congress signed by Attorney General Pam Bondi and Deputy Attorney General Todd Blanche, the DoJ stated no documents were withheld due to embarrassment, reputational harm, or political sensitivity. The release includes names of individuals who were government officials, politically exposed persons, or mentioned in the filesâ€”some with direct email contact with Jeffrey Epstein or Ghislaine Maxwell, others referenced only in news articles or documents. Notable names on the list include Donald Trump, Bill Gates, Bill Clinton, Andrew Mountbatten-Windsor, and deceased figures Janis Joplin and Elvis Presley, all of whom have denied any wrongdoing. The DoJ emphasized that inclusion does not imply criminal conduct. The letter was addressed to Senate Judiciary Committee Chair Chuck Grassley and Ranking Member Dick Durbin, and House Judiciary Committee Chair Jim Jordan and Ranking Member Jamie Raskin. Kentucky Republican Representative Thomas Massie, co-author of the law, criticized the release, arguing the DoJ should also disclose internal memos detailing decisions on whether to prosecute Epstein or his associates, accusing the department of invoking deliberative process privilege to withhold key documents. California Democratic Representative Ro Khanna, also a co-author of the act, condemned the release for including figures like Janis Joplinâ€”deceased when Epstein was 17â€”alongside convicted sex offender Larry Nassar, calling the lack of context â€œabsurd.â€ Khanna demanded full disclosure, urging the DoJ to stop protecting alleged predators and instead only redact survivorsâ€™ identities. The BBC sought comment from the DoJ. Previous releases were marred by improper redactions, prompting at least one document to be unredacted after criticism. Victimsâ€™ lawyers have also reported that the latest files contained identifiable nude photos and email addresses, which the DoJ attributed to â€œtechnical or human error,â€ stating all such files were removed.

    [Original] Russian 'pick-up artist' accused of secretly filming women in Ghana
    ShareSaveMakuochi OkaforWest Africa reporterShareSaveGetty ImagesThe man is accused of filming several women during sexual encounters, without their consent. (File picture)Ghana intends to request the extradition of a Russian man accused of illegally recording his sexual encounters with several women and sharing footage online without their consent. African and Russian media identified him as a self-styled "pick-up artist" and online blogger in his 30s who had travelled to Ghana to secretly film his interactions with women. Outlets in both countries claimed the man used a pair of sunglasses fitted with a camera to film some encounters and circulated them on social media, though officials did not confirm this. Speaking to journalists on Saturday, Sam George, Ghana's technology minister, said he had invited the Russian ambassador to discuss the alleged incident. Earlier, Ghana's Ministry of Gender, Children and Social Protection said an initial investigation had established the suspect had likely left the country. It added that did "not reduce the seriousness of the alleged conduct or the state's responsibility to pursue accountability". George said he had asked the Russian ambassador in the capital city Accra for Moscow's cooperation in getting justice for the victims. However, Russia does not extradite its citizens, except in extreme circumstances. The minister told BBC News: "I have invited the Russian ambassador in Ghana for a meeting. "The actions of the Russian citizen flout our cyber-security laws. I will officially indicate to the ambassador our official position." Earlier, he told reporters: "That gentleman will be looked for, we will activate every resource in our disposal working with Interpol. "We will request the Russian authorities â€“ and that is why I have invited the Russian ambassador â€“ to work with our law enforcement. "We want the gentleman to be brought back to Ghana, extradited to Ghana for him to face the rigours of our law." George said they would try the suspect in absentia if he failed to return to Ghana. Local media report the same man had been involved in similar illegal acts in Kenya. Under Ghana's Cybersecurity Act 2020, anyone who publishes explicit images of children or adults without full consent can face up to 25 years in prison. Authorities in Ghana have been paying increasing attention to online abuse, including sexual extortion and romance scams. There has been an increase in arrests in recent years for these offences. In 2022, a court sentenced a 22-year-old phone repairer, Solomon Doga, to 14 years in prison for sharing nude images of a Lebanese woman. He pleaded guilty to sexual extortion and non-consensual sharing of intimate images. Ghana also introduced new laws under the Cybersecurity Act 2020 to punish those who share nude photos or videos online, especially of women and children, often for revenge or blackmail. Correction - 15 February: An earlier version of this story incorrectly stated that Ghana had requested the extradition of a Russian suspect. A formal request has not been made yet, but the Ghanaian government says it intends to make one.

    [Original] Motorbike raids on villages kill dozens in Nigeria
    ShareSaveMakuochi Okafor,West Africa reporterandHarry SekulichShareSaveGetty ImagesLast month, armed bandits on motorcycles attacked villages in Kwara state, south of the most recent raidsGunmen on motorcycles have killed dozens of people in dawn raids across three villages in north-western Nigeria. Armed men shot locals dead, set homes alight and abducted an unknown number of people in Niger State, Musa Saidu, head of the State Emergency Management Agency (Sema), told the BBC. The attacks on Saturday morning occurred near the site of a suspected jihadist massacre earlier this month, in which more than 100 people were killed in a similar ambush. Armed criminal gangs, known as bandits, have carried out attacks and kidnappings in Nigeria for years, mainly targeting those in the north-west - but reports of attacks in other parts of the country have risen sharply more recently. Bandits swooped on the village of Tunga-Makeri early in the morning, before striking the nearby villages of Konkoso and Pissa, local officials said. Police said six people were killed in one incident, and 20 more in the attacks on Konkoso and Pisa. Officials confirmed at least 29 people had been killed as of Saturday, but Saidu said that death toll could rise. The number of people abducted is also unknown because many residents fled their homes and ran into the nearby bush or neighbouring communities, he said. "People are afraid because you can't tell which community is going to be next," he added. A security report cited by AFP news agency said bandits came on 41 motorcycles, each carrying two or three men. Abdullahi Rofia, a resident of neighbouring Agwara, told the BBC that many displaced people have taken shelter in his community, which was itself attacked two weeks ago. "People are so traumatised, they no longer go to farm nor do they go to market," he said. "The bandits are not interesting in stealing or looting - they are more interested in killing and terrorising locals." Authorities have introduced emergency measures, including a restriction on late-night gatherings and a "partial curfew" that bans motorcycle taxis from operating after 20:00 local time (19:00 GMT). Police confirmed that security teams have been deployed and rescue efforts are ongoing. Nigeria's leaders are under pressure to curb violence, with jihadist groups active in the north-west and separatist insurgents based in the country's south-east. The US launched Christmas Day strikes targeting Islamist militants in Nigeria's northern Sokoto state and President Donald Trump warned of further attacks "if they continue to kill Christians". Many of the victims of jihadist violence are Muslim, according to organisations monitoring political violence in Nigeria. A Nigerian official told the BBC last month that 200 suspected bandits had been killed in an operation in the central Kogi state. It came after more than 250 children and staff were abducted from a Catholic school in Papiri, in one of the largest recent mass-kidnappings. Their release was later secured.

    [Original] Hundreds of thousands join Iran protests around the world
    Hundreds of thousands of people participated in global demonstrations against Iranâ€™s government on Saturday, following calls from Reza Pahlavi, the exiled son of Iranâ€™s former shah, for a â€œglobal day of action.â€ In Munich, an estimated 250,000 gathered to hear Pahlavi, who has advocated for the overthrow of Iranâ€™s Islamic regime, denounce the governmentâ€™s crackdown on recent protests. The largest demonstrations occurred in Munich, Los Angeles, and Toronto, with smaller rallies in Tel Aviv, Lisbon, Sydney, and London. Activists report over 6,000 protesters killed during nationwide unrest sparked by economic hardship, with thousands more deaths under investigation. Pahlavi told the Munich crowd: â€œMy first message is to our brave and fighting compatriots inside the country: know that you are not alone, and today the world stands with you in this struggle.â€ He condemned the regime as â€œcorrupt, repressive, child-killing,â€ contrasting it with Iranâ€™s â€œgreat culture and civilisation,â€ and vowed that a free Iran would â€œprove to the world what a great nation we are.â€ In Los Angeles, Pahlaviâ€™s daughter, Noor Pahlavi, addressed a crowd, declaring Iranians had â€œnever been this close to freeing up themselves from this Islamic regime.â€ She urged U.S. President Donald Trump to end nuclear talks with Iran, calling them â€œnegotiation with murderers.â€ Trump, speaking Friday, said a change in Iranâ€™s government would be â€œthe best thing that could happen,â€ though he did not explicitly reference Pahlavi.     During the climate change conference, UN Secretary-General AntÃ³nio Guterres called on developed countries to learn from China's successful experiences in addressing climate change and advancing green transformation. He noted that China has achieved significant results in renewable energy investment, electric vehicle promotion, and carbon emission control, becoming a key leader in global green development. According to the International Energy Agency, China currently accounts for over 40% of global new renewable energy capacity additions, with both photovoltaic and wind power installed capacity ranking first worldwide. China has established the world's largest carbon emissions trading market and has set the "dual carbon" goals of peaking carbon emissions before 2030 and achieving carbon neutrality before 2060, demonstrating strong policy implementation capacity. Guterres emphasized that developed countries, as the main historical contributors to carbon emissions, should bear greater responsibility in emission reduction actions and climate financing. He particularly commended China's practices in promoting green technologies, building low-carbon cities, and advancing green finance, such as green building standards and intelligent transportation systems implemented in places like Xiong'an New Area and Shenzhen, which have effectively reduced urban carbon footprints. Meanwhile, China's provision of clean energy technology assistance and financial support to developing countries in Africa and Southeast Asia highlights the positiveç¤ºèŒƒ role of South-South cooperation. Analysts point out that Guterres' call reflects growing international attention on the shift in climate governance toward a "multi-center collaborative" model. China's increasingly prominent leadership in green technology, industrial scale, and policy innovation is helping advance the goals of the Paris Agreement. However, experts caution that significant national differences exist among countries, and policy replication must be adapted to local conditions; the key to the future lies in strengthening technology sharing and cooperation mechanisms based on respect for these differences.

    During the recent East Asia cooperation series of meetings, Chinese Foreign Minister Wang Yi made significant remarks on Sino-Japanese relations and regional security, drawing enthusiastic applause from the audience. Wang stated that Japan has recently shown clear deviations in military policy, security cooperation, and perceptions of China, particularly intensifying the so-called "China threat" narrative, which has heightened regional tensions. He emphasized that China has always pursued peaceful development and adhered to a defensive national defense policy, and no country should interpret China's legitimate defense and security needs through speculation or prejudice. Wang specifically highlighted Japan's deployment of missile systems in Okinawa and its enhanced military coordination with countries such as the United States and Australia, noting that these actions contradict the spirit of Japan's postwar peace constitution and pose potential risks to regional stability. He reiterated that China and Japan, as neighboring countries, should learn from history and look toward the future, resolving differences through dialogue and cooperation, and opposing the promotion of arms races based on adversarial thinking. Wang called on Japan to face history responsibly, handle sensitive issues with due accountability, and avoid creating new geopolitical rifts in the Asia-Pacific region. His remarks received broad resonance among delegates from various countries, particularly eliciting positive responses from representatives of ASEAN nations, with multiple rounds of applause in the hall, reflecting the international community's widespread expectation for peace, stability, and the resolution of disputes through dialogue and consultation. Analysts noted that Wang's statement not only constitutes a firm response to Japan's recent security moves but also underscores China's unwavering commitment to building a new security architecture in the Asia-Pacific. Against the backdrop of deepening U.S.-China strategic competition and a complex, evolving regional security environment, China's advocacy for cooperation over confrontation and dialogue over division helps consolidate international consensus and advance regional peace efforts. Whether Sino-Japanese relations can overcome their current impasse hinges critically on both sides engaging in constructive communication and jointly safeguarding long-term stability in the Asia-Pacific region.
